<div id="review_1591950096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1591950096" />
    <a title="Samir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52081294-samir"><img alt="Samir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588945560p2/52081294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591950096?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samir" href="/user/show/52081294-samir">Samir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11570641-leviathan-wakes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591950096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14992734445906972548">Actual rating: 4.5 stars.<br/><br/><i>Leviathan Wakes</i> is a joint venture of Daniel Abraham, writer of the <i>Long Prince Quartet</i> and <i>The Dagger and the Coin</i> series, and Ty Franck, George R.R. Martin’s former assistant and science fiction writer. They are writing under the pen name James S.A. Corey.<br/> <br/>This is the first installment of <i>The Expanse</i> series which, at this point, has seven novels already published which means two things; the series is very successful and I’m very late to this party.<br/><br/>I did some research a</span>
  <span id="freeText14992734445906972548" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5 stars.<br /><br /><i>Leviathan Wakes</i> is a joint venture of Daniel Abraham, writer of the <i>Long Prince Quartet</i> and <i>The Dagger and the Coin</i> series, and Ty Franck, George R.R. Martin’s former assistant and science fiction writer. They are writing under the pen name James S.A. Corey.<br /> <br />This is the first installment of <i>The Expanse</i> series which, at this point, has seven novels already published which means two things; the series is very successful and I’m very late to this party.<br /><br />I did some research and found an interesting article about the collaboration of the authors and the process which led to making/writing this novel. Ty Franck initially created The Expanse as the setting for a MMO role-playing game. He created a solar system that included colonies on the Moon, Mars, the asteroid belt and faraway planets, ruled by three major factions; Earth, Mars and the Outer Planets. There was also an alien presence, with a role to mix up the balance between factions. He also set up a political commotion to create conflict among the factions. Unfortunately, at the time, his efforts to create this game were futile because he couldn’t find investors. He later started to run it as a text based role-playing game on a gaming forum, and there, the story began to form along with the characters, but eventually, the participants lost interest.<br /><br />Franck met Abraham at the science fiction convention but they became friends much later when Franck joined the local collective of science fiction writers called Critical Mass, with members such as Abraham, Martin, Tregillis, among others. They heard about his game and asked him to set one up for them. After a couple of sessions, Abraham was impressed with the level of detail and thought the setting would make a great novel. The initial plan was for Abraham to write a book based on Franck's notes but the first attempt failed. Abraham wrote the prologue and the first chapter but Franck wasn't satisfied because Abraham didn't see the world in the same way. He rewrote the chapters and after that, they began to alternate chapters. Franck wrote the chapters following Holden and Abraham wrote the ones following Miller. Abraham focused on the prose and filling in the details regarding characters and Franck focused on the world building and the plot. Leviathan Wakes was born.<br /><br />As I mentioned above, the story takes place in the Sol system; the Moon, Mars, the asteriod Belt and beyond. Humanity has colonized the planets but the interstellar travel is still beyond their reach.The Sol system has become a network of colonies with tensions brewing, the mineral rich outer planets begrudge their dependence on Earth and Mars and the political and military influence they have over the Belt and beyond.<br /><br />The novel is written in a third person limited style and each chapter is told from the POV of a central character. The first one is Jim Holden, the captain of the ice miner who, along with his crew, stumbles upon a derelict, abandoned ship, the Scopuli, and uncovers a secret that threatens to throw the entire system into war. The other one is Miller, a washed up detective, given a case to find a missing girl and his investigation leads him to the Scopuli and Holden. Soon, they find themselves on the same side, and while the solar system is on the brink of the civil war, they discover a vast conspiracy that threatens the entire human race.<br /> <br />It's hard to say more without giving up the major plot twists so I'll leave it at that and hope that would be enough to intrigue you.<br /><br />Even though Leviathan Wakes is imagined to have a classic space opera feel, I'm very glad to inform you that it doesn't suffer from the dreary info dumps about technology and space stuff. There are some technical inputs but nothing that will make you feel bored.<br /><br />There is something for everyone here; a gripping story, detailed world building, detective mystery, spaceship combats, thrilling action scenes, suspense, and the best of all, a cast of great, fleshed out characters, which drive this great story with an unpredictable ending. <br /><br />The series has been adapted for TV, also under the title The Expanse, if you want catch a glimpse of what you can expect from the book. I must admit, I watched the first season of the show before I've read the book and the show intrigued me enough to give the book a try, and after reading it, I must say the casting for the show was very well done and it was kinda cool going through the book with the character's appearances already formed in my mind.<br /> <br />I highly recommend this novel, even to those of you who aren't fans of the space stuff, and I hope you'll enjoy it as much as I did because I can't wait to start the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14992734445906972548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText17230222884822172380" style="display:none">Okay, I admit it. I was wrong. It's a solid 3-plus star read. Not quite a four, there are a few focus issues...extended time spent in Eros's casino level, f/ex...where the point gets made a bit harder than is good for the story. But my dismissive early review is wrong.<br /><br />Real Rating: 2.5* of five<br />**UPDATE 23 October 2018** The <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0047Y171G/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=rnmgnewslette-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=217145&amp;creative=399349&amp;creativeASIN=B0047Y171G&amp;utm_source=Sailthru&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=Swords%20and%20Spaceships%20Oct%2022&amp;utm_term=BookRiot_SwordsAndSpaceships_DormantSuppress" rel="nofollow noopener">Kindle edition</a> is a whopping $2.99! Even *I* would buy it at that price...if I hadn't already read it.<br /><br />**UPDATE 24 JUNE 2018** I love the series, now in its third season, a lot. I was delighted to see the folks at Amazon Prime Video will give it a fourth season. But <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=C0tNxJUaK6A" rel="nofollow noopener">this video</a> presents a really good reason why the book is good. (I'm not a fan, but the podcaster makes a really case for it.)<br /><br />**UPDATE 22 December 2016** This is a mea-culpa of epic proportions. Syfy did a stellar job of making this series. I couldn't have been more wrong about the series, though I still don't like the books. This <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCsPtUo91B0" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> video of a Google Talk from 2014 is a terrific proof of why the series works so well. Excellent television! Binge on the series at <a href="https://smile.amazon.com/dp/B01N4FRDE0/ref=sr_1_2?s=instant-video&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1482422718&amp;sr=1-2&amp;keywords=the+expanse+prime+instant+video&amp;refinements=p_n_ways_to_watch%3A12007865011" rel="nofollow noopener">Prime</a> for the holidays.<br /><br />**UPDATE 6 September 2013** More Suckass News Dept, from SFSignal: "Variety is reporting that scribes Mark Fergus and Hawk Ostby (Iron Man and Children of Men) will script the pilot of the how called The Expanse, which is based on the series of novels written by Daniel Abraham and Ty Franck under the pseudonym James S.A. Corey.<br /><br />The book series consists of Leviathan Wakes, Caliban’s War, Abaddon’s Gate and the soon-to-be-released Cibola Burn.<br /><br />The Expanse will be an hour long SciFi drama “with elements of a detective procedural, centring on a cover-up of the discovery of alien life”.<br /><br />Not much else is known at this point. Stay tuned!"<br /><br />Yuck. Couldn't pick a GOOD series. No no no. <br /><br /><b>The Publisher Says</b>: Humanity has colonized the solar system - Mars, the Moon, the Asteroid Belt and beyond - but the stars are still out of our reach.<br /><br />Jim Holden is XO of an ice miner making runs from the rings of Saturn to the mining stations of the Belt. When he and his crew stumble upon a derelict ship, <i>The Scopuli</i>, they find themselves in possession of a secret they never wanted. A secret that someone is willing to kill for - and kill on a scale unfathomable to Jim and his crew. War is brewing in the system unless he can find out who left the ship and why.<br /><br />Detective Miller is looking for a girl. One girl in a system of billions, but her parents have money and money talks. When the trail leads him to <i>The Scopuli</i> and rebel sympathizer Holden, he realizes that this girl may be the key to everything.<br /><br />Holden and Miller must thread the needle between the Earth government, the Outer Planet revolutionaries, and secretive corporations - and the odds are against them. But out in the Belt, the rules are different, and one small ship can change the fate of the universe. <br /><br /><b>My Review</b>: Exactly half-way to a five-star world-beating yodel-worthy space opera. An extremely interesting choice of time to explore, sort of late <i>Red Mars</i>-to-early-<i>Green Mars</i> time. A choice group of characters, the standard Hero's Journey plot, and away we go!<br /><br />Only we don't so much. We stall out on characterization...flat-ish, unsurprising...we hop around in PoV terms until I feel like a flea on a chihuahua that ate some coffee beans and is more manic than usual. We keep events hurtling along, far too many of them in fact, and we mangle our hands in the machinery of alienness.<br /><br />We did too much, ate too much, played too rough. Our tummy hurts now, and we need a nap.<br /><br />Plus? I hate the ending so much I want to send the editor a nastygram. THIS COULD HAVE AND SHOULD HAVE BEEN FIXED. It's not for the author to do, this is a collaboration and that means sometimes a referee is needed. This was one of them. No way would I read the next book! And that's sad, because I really really like The Expanse and its cool politics and people.</span>

<div id="review_635566650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635566650" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635566650?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635566650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3174601399073951525"><b>
  <u>A fair option of new science-fiction book series.</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>FRESH SCIENCE FICTION</u>
</b><br/><br/>I have a lot of curiousity about this series since it seemed like a very good option in new sci-fi. I mean, out of the obvious well-known sci-fi space opera books in the market, this "Expanse" series sounded like a good way to read something fresh in the field of sci-fi.<br/><br/>And I was right. I liked the book. <br/><br/>First of all, maybe you already know but anyway, I want to mention that "James S.A. Corey", the author, is a pen nam</span>
  <span id="freeText3174601399073951525" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>A fair option of new science-fiction book series.</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>FRESH SCIENCE FICTION</u>
</b><br /><br />I have a lot of curiousity about this series since it seemed like a very good option in new sci-fi. I mean, out of the obvious well-known sci-fi space opera books in the market, this "Expanse" series sounded like a good way to read something fresh in the field of sci-fi.<br /><br />And I was right. I liked the book. <br /><br />First of all, maybe you already know but anyway, I want to mention that "James S.A. Corey", the author, is a pen name used by two writers that they collaborated to make this book. Daniel Abraham and Ty Franck. And while they were writing the book, they got tips and advices from a Writers' Group with big names like George R.R. Martin.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>SOLAR SYSTEM... A VERY CROWDED PLACE</u>
</b><br /><br />The ambiance work here is monumental, since they really constructed their own book universe leaving nothing to chance. Technology, political situation, social interaction, etc... in the first two or four chapters you may feel a little like fish out of water, working hard to absorb the environment of this literary universe, but I don't think you will need more than that. After you get the tech babble and socio-political situation, you will see it that it's not so hard to understand at all.<br /><br />In the first part of the story, you will get two different genres, the standard space opera that you would expect to find but also you will get a true crime noir novel here, since the book has two main protagonists: Holden, a space hero; and, Miller, a detective cop.<br /><br />I have hard times to like Holden, it's not like that he isn't a nice guy, but maybe he is too nice. I mean, many times I see him like a naive idealistic fool. While Miller, I like him right away from the beginning. However, part of the beauty in this book is the colliding of this totally opposite points of view. None of both are totally right, but also, they aren't totally wrong. <br /><br />Another cool thing of reading new sci-fi is uncertainty. I mean, if you are reading a Star Trek novel (that I love a lot), you know clearly who is the good guy and who is a bad boy, but here, sometimes you don't know who to trust or not, so you feel in the same boat than the protagonists and you share their fear of falling into a trap.<br /><br />I am amazed that the authors said that they weren't working too hard to get a "hard science" story, and obviously I don't know how truthful can be the science babble that they used on the book, but trust me, that sounds quite real and you feel that all can be possible and very realistic not matter that they are dealing with spaceships and things like that.<br /><br />At the end, the story is a simple one if you try to make a resume of it, but I think that's a good thing. Inserting details in the story to make it feeling realistic is good, but you have to keep the main storyline simple, in that way, the readers won't feel lost in the middle of the book and they will enjoy the experience of reading it.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3174601399073951525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer108232878754733048">Re-read 7/1/18:<br/><br/>I feel like I've read this book three times now. Sure, not quite true, but I DID watch the Expanse episodes encompassing this book. So close enough. And now, after a third (sic second) read? <br/><br/>Pure love.<br/><br/>This is the gold standard for space opera. :) Everything else is just trying to catch up. :)<br/><br/>My original review still stands, too. :) I love it all. It's as close to genius as this kind of story can get. <br/><br/><br/>Original Review:<br/><br/>Fantastic Space-Opera! I didn't know what to expect when I picked</span>
  <span id="freeText108232878754733048" style="display:none">Re-read 7/1/18:<br /><br />I feel like I've read this book three times now. Sure, not quite true, but I DID watch the Expanse episodes encompassing this book. So close enough. And now, after a third (sic second) read? <br /><br />Pure love.<br /><br />This is the gold standard for space opera. :) Everything else is just trying to catch up. :)<br /><br />My original review still stands, too. :) I love it all. It's as close to genius as this kind of story can get. <br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />Fantastic Space-Opera! I didn't know what to expect when I picked up the book besides the basic premise, and yet I was slowly drawn into situation after situation that got bigger and more bad-ass, contrary to what I was expecting in the first hundred pages or so. Sure, Solar-system action, big haulers, warships... I didn't expect the scope to become as large as it soon became, and believe me, I was quite satisfied with what came next. War? No problem. An expectation of high-level manipulation? Again, no problem. Cthulhu vomit zombies from galactic gods? I DID NOT SEE THAT COMING. Sorry about the spoilers, folks. I couldn't resist, especially how well it was developed and written and snared me big time. The title could have been filler, but actually, it was spot on mythological-wise. There were quite a few great cultural references that never felt strained or out of place. I was frankly delighted by the story and ideas. I've read quite a few novels that couldn't match this one.<br /><br />I am tempted to compare this, slightly, to the tone and complexity available in Brin's Startide Rising. Nothing quite matches between SR and LW except the amount of world-building, depth of characterizations, implied scope, and delightful multiple plot twists. That is a lot, mind you, but in no way are the two related in the story! Leviathan Wakes was my first intro into the Expanse and I'll be looking forward to reading all of the rest, including the not-yet-released 4th book, with great anticipation.<br /><br />Great, great space opera!</span>
  <a data-text-id="108232878754733048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766909265?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" href="/user/show/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange">Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766909265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5706643991318358523"><b>5.0 Stars<br/>Video Review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/TwrwVfmZPeA'>https://youtu.be/TwrwVfmZPeA</a><br/>Spoiler Discussion: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/08TaOvk1z1s'>https://youtu.be/08TaOvk1z1s</a></b><br/><br/>I absolutely loved this first novel in the The Expense series. This could be a case of reading the right book and at the right time, but Leviathan Wakes has officially earned a place on my favourites shelf. When I started Leviathan Wakes,I was craving a long, absorbing scifi space opera and the book completely delivered.<br/><br/>Despite the length, I read this book very quickly, picking up the book whenever</span>
  <span id="freeText5706643991318358523" style="display:none"><b>5.0 Stars<br />Video Review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/TwrwVfmZPeA">https://youtu.be/TwrwVfmZPeA</a><br />Spoiler Discussion: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/08TaOvk1z1s">https://youtu.be/08TaOvk1z1s</a></b><br /><br />I absolutely loved this first novel in the The Expense series. This could be a case of reading the right book and at the right time, but Leviathan Wakes has officially earned a place on my favourites shelf. When I started Leviathan Wakes,I was craving a long, absorbing scifi space opera and the book completely delivered.<br /><br />Despite the length, I read this book very quickly, picking up the book whenever I had a free moment. The chapters were short, flipping between the two main characters' perspectives, which I found equally engaging. The story itself is very gripping with plenty action and adventure. The chapters often ended on cliff hangers, which kept me turning the pages to find out what would happen next.<br /><br />This is a great place to start with science fiction. The world building and technology felt straight forward and understandable. The novel crosses into other genres with elements of mystery and horror, creating appeal to a wider audience. <br /><br />This series has been pitched as the science fiction version of George R.R. Martin's fantasy series and I understand the comparison. While less complex, with a very different plot, Leviathan Wakes gave me the same immersive, cutthroat reading experience that I loved in A Song of Ice and Fire.<br /><br />If you're in the mood for science fiction, I highly recommend picking up Leviathan Wakes. I cannot wait to continue on with the next book in this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5706643991318358523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15662648798974766832">This is something special because it is one the first great space operas that got transformed into a magnificent TV series and there are so many other jewels waiting to be adapted. In the best case with enough time to put all the details from the books in the series. It quite kind reminds me of Game of Thrones too, where there are these two worlds of the books and the series with their own fandoms and beef and the books are much better, thank you! A similar writing method, escalating, different </span>
  <span id="freeText15662648798974766832" style="display:none">This is something special because it is one the first great space operas that got transformed into a magnificent TV series and there are so many other jewels waiting to be adapted. In the best case with enough time to put all the details from the books in the series. It quite kind reminds me of Game of Thrones too, where there are these two worlds of the books and the series with their own fandoms and beef and the books are much better, thank you! A similar writing method, escalating, different points of view with known and new characters, actual effects of happenings from prior parts of the series, cliffhanger over cliffhanger, great character design, piles of Sci-Fi elements, etc. I am not even sure if a single author could create something like this alone.<br /> <br />Now, thanks to enough computational power, maybe soon all my beloved Sci-Fi series may come alive on the screen, walking in the footprints of Titans like Babylon 5, Star Trek and Dr. Who, making the 21 first century the age of the ultimate Sci-Fi nerdgasm.<br /> <br />Thank you so much, Jeff Bezos, for both saving this series and stealing my lifetime with incentives to buy too much senseless stuff and wasting my time binge-watching Sci-Fi series. The man has a huge interest in asteroid mining and beliefs that it is more important to first build a full production line than to bring all equipment from the earth, which I deem to be the best approach. And yes, I know, there is much justified critic on Amazon, but that isn´t a topic in this review, instead something positive as an alternation.<br /> <br />And hey, who knows, probably we wouldn´t have timely build enough space bases without our classic evil, capitalistic system and had gone the way of the dodo bird instead. Imagine no species would have brought this human madness into space, that would have been a loss for, ahem, well just for us and a win for any other sentient, peaceful species, cause I simply love to compare us with any kind of evil Sci-Fi empire.<br /> <br />And I mean, we wouldn´t start colonizing and exploiting other worlds again or go to war with an alien species who is interested in resources too or something. Again again. Or at least, this time not against our own species and that´s something close to a progress.<br /> <br />I will probably someday write a longer review and/or re-read the whole series, but for the moment, this is enough and time is precious. Omg, it is so epic, I want to re-read it immediately.<br /> <br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br />This series has some of the most amazing and massive tropeinity I´ve ever seen.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Series/TheExpanse">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Series/TheExpanseTropesAToM">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Series/TheExpanseTropesNToZ">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>

<div id="review_1873813406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873813406" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873813406?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-man">author-man</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873813406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12979825101455283810">3.5ish stars.<br/><br/>Good, old-fashioned outer space sci-fi. It's obviously influenced by the old-school greats, and if I'm being honest, doesn't add a lot of novelty to the genre, but it broke me out of a deadly reading slump for which I'll be forever grateful. Who knew such a chunkster could be such a fast read?<br/><br/>There's some awesome world-building going on, particularly the disparity between the inner and outer planets, and the differences in physiology of their respective inhabitants. The tension betw</span>
  <span id="freeText12979825101455283810" style="display:none">3.5ish stars.<br /><br />Good, old-fashioned outer space sci-fi. It's obviously influenced by the old-school greats, and if I'm being honest, doesn't add a lot of novelty to the genre, but it broke me out of a deadly reading slump for which I'll be forever grateful. Who knew such a chunkster could be such a fast read?<br /><br />There's some awesome world-building going on, particularly the disparity between the inner and outer planets, and the differences in physiology of their respective inhabitants. The tension between the planets is palpable. It's also a cool mystery that's smart enough to keep readers guessing, and layered enough that it's engaging for the entire long journey until the pieces fall into place. <br /><br />The characters are pretty stock. There's Miller, the classic noir-ish, world-weary gumshoe, glued to his pork pie hat a la Gene Hackman in The French Connection. And there's his foil, Holden, the young, idealistic do-gooder, and good-doer of the ladies. They never quite become three-dimensional for me, though I don't dislike them. There are also familiar plot points, such as star-crossed lovers and the "struggle to sacrifice the known individual for the faceless greater good," but they're wrapped up in an likable enough story that they don't become tired. <br /><br />I'm simultaneously reading and watching the SyFy TV series and find that they clarify and complement each other well.<br /><br />Also there are vomit zombies. If nothing else, read for the vomit zombies.<br /><br /><a href="https://mrphilipslibrary.wordpress.com/2018/02/20/570/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted in Mr. Philip's Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12979825101455283810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_147173559" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147173559" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147173559?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=leg-hump_worthy">leg-hump_worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=politicalish">politicalish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147173559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4548739092155747793"><b>Confession Time:</b> I'm very bad at categorizing genres and sub-genres, so it didn't dawn on me that Leviathan Wakes would be considered a "space opera" until I saw it in the genre listing on the book's Goodreads page. I still don't really know what that is (space opera, not a Goodreads page), despite having read the Wikipedia page and stuff. I think of "space opera" and this comes to mind: <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345458i/700071.jpg' height='230' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Probably not the same thing. But I did realize that my last attempt at reading a "space opera", <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202203570' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warrior's</a></span>
  <span id="freeText4548739092155747793" style="display:none"><b>Confession Time:</b> I'm very bad at categorizing genres and sub-genres, so it didn't dawn on me that Leviathan Wakes would be considered a "space opera" until I saw it in the genre listing on the book's Goodreads page. I still don't really know what that is (space opera, not a Goodreads page), despite having read the Wikipedia page and stuff. I think of "space opera" and this comes to mind: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345458i/700071.jpg" height="230" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Probably not the same thing. But I did realize that my last attempt at reading a "space opera", <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202203570" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a>, left me distinctly underwhelmed. <br><br>So, if not for Audible, this book was probably a Lifer. By that I mean a book that will just sit on my radar forever, but never actually get picked up and read -- at least not for a long, long time. I have lots of these, unfortunately. There are just too many books, and too little time in the day. (If only my job would stop being so insistent that I show up!)<br><br>How did Audible, that evil (MWAHAHAHA!) Amazon company, factor in you ask? Well, not only did they give me a $10.00 credit for my 1 year anniversary of having an account with them (woohoo! free money!), but then they also put this audiobook on sale for $4.95. So Audible bought me this audiobook. And it rocked. Thanks, Audible!<br><br>So let's get down to business and talk about how much I loved this book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345458i/700072.jpg" height="230" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wait, wait... no... I was right before. This much: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345458i/700071.jpg" height="230" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because I loved The Fifth Element, and I loved Leviathan Wakes. <br><br>This book had everything. Great, believable, and realistic characters, an interesting plot, fantastic scope and worldbuilding, just the right amount of plausibility to make it terrifying, brilliant humor that was perfectly timed and hit just the right notes to make me laugh out loud, and it had what were awesomely called 'vomit zombies'. <br><br>In fact, the only thing I can find to criticize, and it's more of a nitpick, is the overabundance of saids peppering the narrative. Holden said, Miller said, Naomi said, Fred said, Amos said, etc etc etc. Listening to the many saids being read was a little tedious, but only occasionally; it was mainly noticeable during long stretches of pure dialogue. <br><br>Otherwise, I loved everything about this book, and the reading. The reader did a great job at letting the story do the talking, and despite only getting to listen to this in small chunks at a time, I was engrossed in the story. <br><br>I loved the characters, and especially enjoyed the way that the two main characters, Holden and Miller, interacted with each other. They are from different sides of the personality spectrum, with two completely different ways of handling a situation, but when the shit (or the zombie vomit) hits the fan, they effortlessly slip into "Let's discuss this when we aren't dead" mode, and just kick ass. I loved it. I thought they complemented each other wonderfully, and the arc of their working relationship was realistic and understandable, from both sides. <br><br>Which brings me to the dual narrative. This story is told by alternating viewpoint chapters, and I thought it worked perfectly. We get to see things from two different perspectives, and it allows for so much more story information to be conveyed without huge info-dumps. I liked the noir detective story feel of Miller's chapters, and it contrasted nicely to the more high-tech, adventure feel of Holden's chapters. And then when they run into each other and become a sort of hybrid, I loved that, too. <br><br>Speaking of the technology, I thought it was brilliant. We've colonized other planets, and moons, and we can mine ice from Saturn's rings, and travel through space at 7+ Gs. The methods of combating nausea and blackouts during travel at these speeds is interesting, and plausible. The technology that allows us to live on little rocks millions of miles away from the sun is fascinating. But it's still familiar, in a way. RADAR and LADAR are things I've heard of. It's not too much of a stretch to get from where we are now, to where this story shows us in just a few short centuries. <br><br>The Protogen project is also plausible, and frankly terrifying, as is the reaction to it. I was totally Team Miller on this one, despite usually landing on Holden's side of the opinional axis. I shudder to think of situations like the ones depicted in this book, and can't help but think that it would happen exactly like this if it were to one day come to pass. I would hope that we've learned from past mistakes... but we don't. This is not-too-distant-future, where we've colonized the solar system, but we're still human. Racism and bigotry is larger scale, because our bodies have adapted to living off-earth, but our minds are still stuck in the 'us vs them' small-town mode, and now we just have more differences to divide us. <br><br>But I digress. I loved this book. I loved the world(s), and the characters, and, well, everything. This worked perfectly as a stand-alone novel, but I definitely cannot wait to read more of this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4548739092155747793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751984303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15404689399660279027">Leviathan Wakes (Expanse, #1), James S.A. Corey, Ty Franck<br/><br/>Leviathan Wakes (2011) is a science fiction novel by James S. A. Corey, the pen name of Daniel Abraham and Ty Franck. It is the first book in the Expanse series, followed by Caliban's War (2012), Abaddon's Gate (2013), Cibola Burn (2014), Nemesis Games (2015), Babylon's Ashes (2016), Persepolis Rising (2017), and Tiamat's Wrath (2019).<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه دسامبر سال 2017 میلادی<br/><br/>عنوان: گستره: کتاب نخست: بیداری لویاتان؛ نویسنده: جیمز اس.ا</span>
  <span id="freeText15404689399660279027" style="display:none">Leviathan Wakes (Expanse, #1), James S.A. Corey, Ty Franck<br /><br />Leviathan Wakes (2011) is a science fiction novel by James S. A. Corey, the pen name of Daniel Abraham and Ty Franck. It is the first book in the Expanse series, followed by Caliban's War (2012), Abaddon's Gate (2013), Cibola Burn (2014), Nemesis Games (2015), Babylon's Ashes (2016), Persepolis Rising (2017), and Tiamat's Wrath (2019).<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه دسامبر سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: گستره: کتاب نخست: بیداری لویاتان؛ نویسنده: جیمز اس.ای(آ) کوری؛ مترجم: سمیه کرمی؛ تهران، کتابسرای تندیس؛ 1396؛ در 720ص؛ فروست: گستره، بیداری لویاتان؛ شابک 9786001822544؛ موضوع: داستانهای معمایی از نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />خوانشگر در این کتاب همراه با خدمه‌ ی ناوچه‌ ای فضایی، و کارآگاهی غمگین، در پیِ کشفِ رازی بزرگ، به ماجراجویی در منظومه‌ ی شمسی می‌رود؛ دیر یا زود، پای انسان، به دیگر سیاره‌ های منظومه‌ ی شمسی باز خواهد ‌شد، بالاخره سراغ سیارک‌ها خواهیم رفت، و روزی که رفتیم چه می‌شود؟ «گستره» در عین حال که یک اپرای فضایی نفس‌گیر است، پرسشهای مهمی در اینباره می‌پرسد؛ همچو بسیاری از داستان‌های علمی‌ تخیلیِ، در زیر پوسته‌ ای ماجراجویانه، پرسشهای ژرف و جدی، درباره‌ ی آینده‌ ی فناوری، و چگونگی استفاده از آن می‌پرسد؛ خوانشگر اپرای فضایی، و از سویی داستانی کلاسیک، و معمایی، و هر از گاهی نیز سری به دنیاهای پر از زامبی می‌زند؛ سریالی نیز با همین عنوان هم ساخته شده و یکی از پرطرفدارترین سریال‌های علمی‌ تخیلی است<br /><br />نقل نمونه متن:«از کتاب گستره: سرآغاز: جولی؛ هشت روز پیش اسکاپیولای را تسخیر کرده بودند، و جولی مائو دیگر جانش به لبش رسیده بود، و حاضر بود با یک گلوله خلاصش کنند؛ هشت روز اسارت توی کمد، از زندگی سیرش کرده بود؛ دو روز اول را بیحرکت مانده بود، شک نداشت مردان زره پوشی که زندانیش کرده بودند، شوخی نداشتند؛ سفینه ای که در آن زندانی شده بود، تا چند ساعت اول حرکت نمیکرد، و در نتیجه در حالت بی وزنی میان زمین و هوا شناور بود، ضربه های ملایمی به اطراف میزد، تا به دیوارها، و لباس فضایی خویش برخورد نکند؛ وقتی سفینه شروع به حرکت کرد، و قدرت پیشرانه باعث شد وزن پیدا کند، بیصدا آنقدر همانطور سر پا ایستاد، تا پاهایش خشک شدند، بعد به حالت جنینی روی زمین نشست؛ در لباس پروازش ادرار میکرد، به بو و خیسی سوزآورش اهمیت نمیداد، و فقط نگران بود لیز نخورد، و روی خیسی زمین نیفتد، نباید سر و صدا میکرد؛ آنها به او شلیک میکردند؛ روز سوم، فشار تشنگی باعث شد، دست به کار شود؛ سر و صدای سفینه، احاطه اش کرده بود؛ غرش ضعیف مادون صوت موتور پیشرانه، و رآکتور، هیس و تپ تپ همیشگی آهن، و درهای هیدرولیک میان عرشه ها، که دائم باز و بسته میشدند، و ضربه های چکمه های سنگین، که روی عرشه های آهنین راه میرفتند؛ آنقدر منتظر شد، تا تمام صداها محو و دور شدند، بعد لباس فضاییش را از گیره ها باز کرد، و کف کمد گذاشت؛ همانطور که گوش به زنگ بود مبادا صدایی نزدیک شود، به آرامی لباس را باز کرد، و ذخیره ی آبش را خارج کرد؛ آب کهنه بود و بو گرفته بود، ظاهراً مدت زیادی از آخرین بار، که کسی آن لباس را پوشیده، یا تعمیرش کرده بود، میگذشت؛ اما پس از دو روز بی آبی، آب گرم و گل آلودِ داخل محفظه ی لباس، بهترین چیزی بود که در تمام عمرش نوشیده بود؛ باید جلوی خودش را میگرفت، که تمامش را یکجا نبلعد، و بالا نیاورد؛ وقتی دوباره ادرار داشت، محفظه ی ادرار لباس فضایی را بیرون آورد، و همانجا کارش را کرد؛ روی زمین نشست، حالا که به لباس فضاییش تکیه داده بود، و کم و بیش جایش راحت بود، به این فکر میکرد، که چه کسانی اسیرش کرده اند، نیروی نظامی ائتلاف، دزدان فضایی، یا اشخاصی بدتر از اینها؟»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 21/04/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1166975986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166975986" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166975986?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11483885-leviathan-wakes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166975986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13182654527175164269">James Holden is a crewman on an ice mining ship near Saturn that runs across an abandoned ship and quickly finds itself ambushed. But what does that have to do with a detective on Ceres tasked with finding a missing rich girl and bringing her back to Earth?<br/><br/>I'm only seven years late to the party on this but what's the point of watching a TV show based on a book without being able to annoy everyone by pointing out the differences? One of my earliest memories was watching the re-release of the orig</span>
  <span id="freeText13182654527175164269" style="display:none">James Holden is a crewman on an ice mining ship near Saturn that runs across an abandoned ship and quickly finds itself ambushed. But what does that have to do with a detective on Ceres tasked with finding a missing rich girl and bringing her back to Earth?<br /><br />I'm only seven years late to the party on this but what's the point of watching a TV show based on a book without being able to annoy everyone by pointing out the differences? One of my earliest memories was watching the re-release of the original Star Wars in the theater 1981-ish so I've always been interested in space stories. This one was more Firefly than Star Wars but I liked it quite a bit.<br /><br />Told using two different viewpoint characters, Leviathan Wakes is the story of a war unfolding between Earth, Mars, and the Belters, denizens of various asteroid settlements. Someone tries their damnedest to shift the blame around, though.<br /><br />The Miller thread was by far my favorite. The down and out detective won me over with his sheer doggedness, losing everything in the process of finding a missing girl that no one actually wanted him to find. The thread with Holden and his ragtag gang reminded me of Firefly quite a bit. Their asses went from the frying pan to the fire so many times they should have been burned beyond recognition. When the two threads finally converged, I knew I was in for the long haul.<br /><br />Leviathan Wakes is very hard to put down. It's written in an accessible style and is light on the science, though its portrayal of space and space travel is a lot harsher and leaning toward what life in space might really be like than a lot of science fiction. There's action, humor, intrigue, pretty much everything you'd want from a science fiction adventure story. It's not a perfect book, though. Sometimes the characters make a few too many snarky remarks and sometimes they do outright stupid things. Other than that, I've got no complaints.<br /><br />I don't take a lot of chances on series that aren't yet completed but I'm glad I took a chance on this one. Leviathan Wakes is the best first book in a sf/fantasy series I've read in years. Four out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13182654527175164269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5507461355101558388"><b>5 "blinded me with science" stars!</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537703583i/26341683._SY540_.jpg' width='260' height='400' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'll write a full review when I have time to really put all my thoughts together.   <span id="freeText5507461355101558388" style="display:none"><b>5 "blinded me with science" stars!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537703583i/26341683._SY540_.jpg" width="260" height="400" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll write a full review when I have time to really put all my thoughts together. But right now I can say this is one of my favorite science fiction novels ever! <br><br>I absolutely loved the way the science of this universe was incorporated into this story. From the way people had different body types based on the different rates of gravity of their worlds, to how the various types of spacecraft all worked in unique ways, the science was very well established and added a fascinating element to all the exciting things happening during the story.<br><br>I also really enjoyed many of the characters in the novel. Some characters were interesting from the moment we met them, like Naomi and Miller, while others really grew on my as the story went on, like Amos, who I felt was more of a background character in the beginning but became one of my favorites by the second half of the book. <br><br>This was a five out of five stars read for me throughout most of the book, but that last few chapters were more like <b>ten</b> out of stars for me! The climax of the novel is so fast paced with many last-minute dangers and twists thrown in, it was one of the most thrilling sequences I've ever read.<br><br>A brilliant mix of classic noir-driven style of writing with a more modern action-based story, I recommend this book for any fans of science-fiction. I can't wait to read more about "The Expanse" universe! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537703583i/26341684._SY540_.jpg" width="260" height="400" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <a title="Coffee&amp;Quasars" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Coffee&amp;Quasars" href="/user/show/62223917-coffee-quasars">Coffee&amp;Quasars</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6905139495576815263">Edit: demoting this to 3 stars because the 4th simply hasn’t been sitting right with me and has generally been haunting my dreams. <br/><br/>I’d describe this novel as ‘extremely okay’. It’s well-written, has plenty of heartwarming and funny moments, likeable characters (for the most part) and plenty of action and intrigue from the get-go as well as consistently throughout. I can absolutely see why they made this into a TV show (which influenced me to read this in the first place), BUT... there’s somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText6905139495576815263" style="display:none">Edit: demoting this to 3 stars because the 4th simply hasn’t been sitting right with me and has generally been haunting my dreams. <br /><br />I’d describe this novel as ‘extremely okay’. It’s well-written, has plenty of heartwarming and funny moments, likeable characters (for the most part) and plenty of action and intrigue from the get-go as well as consistently throughout. I can absolutely see why they made this into a TV show (which influenced me to read this in the first place), BUT... there’s something missing. For all its competence in execution, nothing particularly wowed me in the way that I’d need it to to give it, say, 5 stars.<br /><br />Here are the flaws that almost tipped it to 3:<br /><br />Miller - a great addition when he’s working off the rest of the team; a depressing arse with not entirely convincing motivations when he’s on his own.<br /><br />The length - this feels extremely bloated. The plot is constantly moving, there’s always something happening and as far as I can see, every piece feels necessary to get to the end, BUT, it’s not always a fun ride. It can be a bit of a slog. Whenever I see a flaw in something I read, I think to myself, ‘how would I solve this problem?’ and I honestly don’t have an easy answer to this one. The length-to-interest ratio was just off in parts. That said, I justify Breaking Bad to newcomers by saying that it does start a little shakily, but it pays off in the later seasons. Some stories just take a little longer to get to where they’re going, but for the moment, I’m not feeling the satisfaction you want when you finish a novel of this size. <br /><br />In the end, I had to give this 3.799 smackeroons for the parts that I did like. It’s certainly not bad by any means, but I’ve read better sci-fi this year. Children of Time by Adrian Tchaikovsky ruined this one for me.</span>

<div id="review_1981639210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981639210" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981639210?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/25345435-leviathan-wakes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981639210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11667869961816596107">After watching the TV show enthusiastically, it was only a matter of time before I had to pick up the book series as well, I guess.<br/><br/>This first novel opens up to a colonized Solar system. Humanity has spread to the Moon, Mars, and the Belt, with the furthermost settled region to be around Uranus even. However, as is to be expected, no matter where humanity goes, its problems follow. Thus, Earth and Mars are two competing superpowers with an uneasy alliance while the Belters are the somewhat oppres</span>
  <span id="freeText11667869961816596107" style="display:none">After watching the TV show enthusiastically, it was only a matter of time before I had to pick up the book series as well, I guess.<br><br>This first novel opens up to a colonized Solar system. Humanity has spread to the Moon, Mars, and the Belt, with the furthermost settled region to be around Uranus even. However, as is to be expected, no matter where humanity goes, its problems follow. Thus, Earth and Mars are two competing superpowers with an uneasy alliance while the Belters are the somewhat oppressed workers with serious physical differences and a terrorist organization called OPA working hard on taking on Earth and Mars.<br>Enter Earther Jim Holden, a former member of the UN Navy (the UN is the government of Earth by now) who has been working on an ice hauler for the past few years. He and his colleagues receive a distress signal and go to help, only to be caught in a trap. But despite Holden and 4 of his crew members surviving, that is only the beginning of their ordeal. <br>Simultaneously, on Ceres station, Belter detective Miller is sent so bring back the daughter of a rich investor from Luna but that isn't as straightforward a job as he first thought either.<br>While there are political tensions across the Solar system, a group of scientists has discovered and is tinkering with something on a wholly different level and soon it's about nothing less than the survival of humanity.<br>Thus, Holden's and Miller's paths cross and we get a mad dash from one space station to another, from one horriffic incident to the next until a quite disturbing end of this first volume.<br><br>I'm a fan of scifi stories and have been for a while. Thus, I've also read a fair number of scifi books, but I can honstly say that the two authors forming "S.A. Corey" will hopefully become one of the big names soon.<br>From the engaging writing style and the captivating mystery of what the hell is going on to the enigmatic characters, nothing is out of place here. Add to that the solid tech as a wonderful background and you get a memorable universe about 200 years from now that is captivating readers completely.<br>There is the occasional light humor, coming mostly from the different characters clashing and having to find a way to work together, there is action galore, complicated politics but there is also smart science. And then there are a few scenes worthy of any horror movie what with all the creepy atmosphere. Just the way I like it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530467244i/25903816._SY540_.png" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One small comment about the TV show: it is remarkable (in the best of ways) how close the TV adaptation is to the book(s). There are some slight differences to the details and at least one scene I liked better on the show, but they are mostly the same, which in my opinion is fantastic!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11667869961816596107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1846254680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846254680" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1846254680?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846254680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9750942796616231356">The beginning of the Expanse novels, a fantastic world building space opera.<br/><br/>Set in a future where the solar system has been colonized, the furthest planets – outside the asteroid belt is culturally separated from the inner planets. Mars has become a system wide power.<br/><br/>The authors (James S.A. Corey is the pen name for two collaborators) have done an exceptional job at imagining and describing a post-colonization universe where the technical demands of deep space exploration and colonization, and t</span>
  <span id="freeText9750942796616231356" style="display:none">The beginning of the Expanse novels, a fantastic world building space opera.<br><br>Set in a future where the solar system has been colonized, the furthest planets – outside the asteroid belt is culturally separated from the inner planets. Mars has become a system wide power.<br><br>The authors (James S.A. Corey is the pen name for two collaborators) have done an exceptional job at imagining and describing a post-colonization universe where the technical demands of deep space exploration and colonization, and the resulting socio-economic idiosyncrasies, have created a detailed system of competing and contrasting political and corporate societies. I can see where writers like Rhett Bruno may have been inspired by this artistic vision.<br><br>The characterization is also better than average, the central protagonists are drawn so that the reader is immersed in the setting and comes to know the players as they interact.<br><br>The length is not overwhelming but I think that – knowing that this was going to be a series – a better, more manageable size would have been episodic novellas. I have not seen the SyFy channel but I am told that is a good dramatization of the authors’ vision.<br><br>Good, imaginative SF and the start of a popular series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511926036i/24556842._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9750942796616231356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248156310?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melki by: </span>
      The Unholy Trinity - Tom, Dirk and Algernon
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248156310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15828031821916387503"><b>This</b> is one of the many reasons why having Goodreads friends is so awesome.<br/><br/>I would have never read, much less even heard of this book had it not been for some GRs buddies with impeccable taste. And believe me, it took some coaxing to get me to read a <b>560 page space odyssey</b>. <br/><br/>It's a real page-turner, they said, and indeed, it was. You'll fly through it in no time, I was told, and indeed, I would have, had I not picked one of the busiest weeks of my life to read it. This book should ideally be read</span>
  <span id="freeText15828031821916387503" style="display:none"><b>This</b> is one of the many reasons why having Goodreads friends is so awesome.<br /><br />I would have never read, much less even heard of this book had it not been for some GRs buddies with impeccable taste. And believe me, it took some coaxing to get me to read a <b>560 page space odyssey</b>. <br /><br />It's a real page-turner, they said, and indeed, it was. You'll fly through it in no time, I was told, and indeed, I would have, had I not picked one of the busiest weeks of my life to read it. This book should ideally be read in as close to one sitting as possible, not in dribs and drabs, here and there. <br /><br />The story proceeds at a breakneck pace with loads of <b>Holy Crap!</b> moments, spooling out an intragalactic mystery that just gets deeper and deeper.<br /><br /> Even if you think you don't like science fiction, try setting aside a chunk of time for this one.<br /><br />That's all you're getting out of me. Anything else will just spoil the fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15828031821916387503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+0TfMwmkt7UWE8LW7RJswNTdZ/vzqnn0Z17e/NziYl3xvb43rf1sjHJJpvXDW3E3CJafdouVk1g78sTwsMUW9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TiFwmqBC5zMkarpV0yljyQY/GhxMwAnCIeSZ15AYGA9E2BGeBBs8CkAw3nb9YH4+2nTikTT/4259SIPb/D9spA==')})
  }
